# Section IV — B122 Architectural Thresh (Directed Processing, Assignments Bank, Aggregate Bounty Exchange)

---


## #2296a (B122-original #2293) Directed Processing & Stagger Ensemble

## INNOVATION_THRESH — #2293 Directed Processing + Stagger Ensemble (CPU-Time-Slicing Analog)

**Innovation:** #2293 — Directed Processing (attention-routing) + Immutable-Fact Grounding + Ensemble Churn (parallel OR single-AI-staggered) → Correctness-Ceiling Approach for AI Reasoning
**Bishop Session:** B122, 2026-04-24 (Founder-ratified as "standalone 2290-sequel class"). Thresh drafted B123.
**Author:** Bishop (Claude Opus 4.7, 1M context), Founder-articulated and ratified in-session
**Filing:** Prov 14 supplementary (thresh-as-we-go; window extended)
**Publication hold:** IN FORCE until Prov 14 receipt
**Related anchors:** #2269 Three Fates, #2278 Cathedral Effect (direct-WHERE-to-process), #2287 Synapses (grounding), #2288 Tribunal (multi-agent ensemble), #2289 Cerberus (retrospective multi-head), #2291 Self-Indexing Scribes (grounding-by-corpus), #2292 CFP (federation substrate).

---

## TL;DR (2 lines)

**A method for approaching the correctness-ceiling of AI reasoning by composing three primitives — (1) routing attention to the right knowledge subset, (2) grounding on immutable facts, (3) ensemble churn — where the ensemble-churn primitive includes a novel single-AI-stagger embodiment (same model, same prompt, varied framings in fast sequence) that achieves ensemble quality on cheaper tiers.** The CPU-time-slicing analogy is the mechanism-proof: a computer doesn't really do everything at once; it does it in sequence so fast it looks simultaneous. Apply the same principle to reasoning.

---

## The Problem

Classical ensemble approaches to AI reasoning require multiple separate model calls (Opus + Sonnet + Haiku, or three independent Sonnets). Cost: 3× API, 3× latency (parallel) or N×3 (serial). Multi-tier ensembles further require provisioning multiple vendor relationships.

Meanwhile, single-model-single-call reasoning leaves quality on the table — even when routing and grounding are optimized (Cathedral Effect #2278 + Self-Indexing Scribes #2291), a single-pass answer is constrained by the model's one-shot compose step.

**The gap**: a unified protocol that composes direction, grounding, and ensemble-churn — with ensemble-churn generalized to include single-AI-staggered runs, so the cheapest usable model tier can deliver ensemble-class output.

---

## The Mechanism

### Four-part claim structure

| Part | Function | Existing LB primitive |
|---|---|---|
| **1. Direct attention** | Route to the right subset of knowledge | Three Fates + Cathedral Effect (#2278) |
| **2. Ground on verified facts** | Immutable-fact injection prevents hallucination within context | Self-Indexing Scribes (#2291), Synapses (#2287) |
| **3. Ensemble churn — parallel** | Multi-agent verification on the directed/grounded problem | Tribunal (#2288), Cerberus (#2289) |
| **4. Ensemble churn — single-AI stagger** | Sequential re-run by the SAME agent with varied framings — **NEW B122 sub-claim** | The novel embodiment |

### The CPU-time-slicing mechanism-proof

**Founder, B122 (verbatim keystone):** *"A computer doesn't really do everything at once, it just does it in sequence so fast that it looks like instantaneous to the human eye."*

Apply the principle to reasoning: one model making three fast staggered calls (each with a distinct frame) on the same question is ensemble-equivalent to three models making parallel calls. The apparent concurrency of traditional ensembles is a convenience, not a requirement. Sequence suffices when speed is high enough.

### Single-AI-stagger embodiments (protect in claims)

1. **Sequential self-critique**: Run 1 = answer. Run 2 = critique Run 1. Run 3 = refine from critique. Final answer from Run 3.
2. **Frame-rotation**: same question, N frames (analytical / skeptical / synthetic). Combine.
3. **Role-rotation**: same question, N personas within same model. Reduce single-perspective blind spots.
4. **Temperature-rotation**: low T = precise; mid T = creative; high T = exhaustive. Combine.

### Cost structure (the economic claim)

Three-call stagger on cheapest tier = typically cheaper than single-call on expensive tier, with ensemble-class quality. Especially relevant at the Haiku-class economics documented in R10 Eyewitness (#2278 Exhibit B) — Haiku ties Opus HOT at 19× cost delta.

---

## Claim Skeleton (5 claims for conversion refinement)

**Claim 1.** A method for approaching the correctness-ceiling of an AI reasoning system, comprising: (a) directing the system's attention to a subset of knowledge relevant to the input, via a routing layer; (b) grounding the system's output on immutable verified facts, via injection of canonical sources into the context window; (c) churning the system through an ensemble of reasoning passes; (d) composing the ensemble outputs into a final answer.

**Claim 2.** The method of claim 1 wherein the ensemble of claim 1(c) comprises multiple independent model calls operating in parallel on the directed and grounded input.

**Claim 3.** The method of claim 1 wherein the ensemble of claim 1(c) is produced by a SINGLE model making MULTIPLE sequentially-staggered calls on the directed and grounded input, with each call parameterized by a distinct frame, role, temperature, or critique-step, such that the ensemble-equivalent output is produced without requiring multiple distinct models or multiple vendor relationships.

**Claim 4.** The method of claim 3 wherein the sequential-stagger embodiment is selected from: (a) sequential self-critique (answer → critique → refine), (b) frame-rotation (analytical / skeptical / synthetic), (c) role-rotation (multiple personas), (d) temperature-rotation (precision / creativity / exhaustiveness).

**Claim 5.** The method of claim 3 wherein the cost of the ensemble is N × per-call cost on the cheapest model tier sufficient for the reasoning task, and wherein said cost is competitive with or lower than a single call on the next-most-expensive tier of the same model family, such that ensemble-class output quality is achievable without escalating model tier.

---

## Empirical validation pathway

- **K477** proved the direction + grounding primitives at +68pp HOT on Cranewell auto-only (injection pathway). Single-AI-stagger not yet tested.
- **Proposed K482+ test**: rerun K477 Iteration C with 3-call single-AI stagger (same Haiku, frame-rotation). If aggregate HOT climbs above 80% HOT toward the 94% MCP-native ceiling, the single-AI-stagger sub-claim is empirically confirmed.
- **Assignments Bank (#2294)** once live: stagger-variant of Assignment #001 available as a member-executable bounty.

---

## Commercial value proposition

CJ-class IP value at the protocol layer. Commercial realization in:

- **Helm PWA** "precision mode" toggle — default single-call, optional 3-call stagger on same tier (cost-preserving alternative to tier-escalation)
- **librarian-mcp-public `--precision` CLI flag** — members get stagger-ensemble on their chosen model via one flag
- **Pledge-eligible** (#2260): the protocol itself is commons; commercial value is in implementations, routing services, integration tooling

---

## Relationships / distinctions

| Layer | Role |
|---|---|
| **Tribunal (#2288)** | Multi-agent live verification — generalist Critics; domain accidental |
| **Cerberus (#2289)** | Retrospective multi-head examination — post-completion |
| **#2293 Directed Processing + Stagger** | Production-time protocol composing attention + grounding + (parallel OR single-AI-stagger) ensemble — covers the gap between Tribunal (multi-agent parallel) and single-model-single-call |

#2293 is the composition-protocol over #2278, #2287, #2291, #2288, #2289; it is not a sub-claim under any of them. Standalone CJ per Founder B122 ratification.

---

## Open Questions for Founder

1. **Name**: "Directed Processing + Stagger Ensemble" is Bishop's working name; Founder-voice alternative? ("Time-Sliced Reasoning," "Sequential Ensemble," etc.)
2. **Claim scope**: should Claim 3 specify minimum N for single-AI-stagger, or leave it as "multiple" for flexibility at conversion?
3. **Filing timing**: Prov 14 current window or accumulate further thresh before file? ("I have learned to wait.")
4. **Empirical gate for public claim**: do we hold public-facing discussion of the single-AI-stagger sub-claim until K482 confirms empirically, or announce with K477's grounding+direction evidence plus CPU-slicing analogy?
5. **Helm PWA surfacing**: ship "precision mode" in v1 or defer to v2 after empirical validation?

---

*End of CJ #2293 skeleton. Awaiting Founder rewrite and ratification.*


---


## #2297a (B122-original #2294) Specific-General Assignments Bank

## INNOVATION_THRESH — #2294 Assignments Bank: Specific-General Bounty Market for Empirical Commons

**Innovation:** #2294 — Assignments Bank: A Repository of Specific Execution-Ready Protocols (Assignments) Claimable by Any Member for Bounty Payment, with Install-as-Demo Onboarding, Three-Tier Sharing/Monetization, and Discovery-Not-Pitch Matching
**Bishop Session:** B122, 2026-04-24 (Founder-proposed and ratified in-session). Thresh drafted B123.
**Author:** Bishop (Claude Opus 4.7, 1M context)
**Filing:** Prov 14 supplementary (thresh-as-we-go; window extended)
**Publication hold:** IN FORCE until Prov 14 receipt
**Related anchors:** #2260 Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge, #2278 Cathedral Effect, #2291 Self-Indexing Scribes, #2292 CFP, #2295 Aggregate Bounty Exchange.

---

## TL;DR (2 lines)

**A bounty-backed market of execution-ready research protocols (Assignments), each drawn from a general catalog (the Bank), where any member can claim → run → submit results for payment, with install-time auto-demo (Assignment #001 runs on user's chosen AI during first-run) and three-tier sharing/monetization ($0 private / $60 share-only / $5/yr full member) — turning self-reported AI benchmarks into third-party-replicated commons evidence by construction.** The peer-review flywheel rebuilt as an open, self-selecting bounty market.

---

## The Problem

Internal AI benchmarks are structurally discount-able: "of course your numbers look good, you ran them." Traditional peer-review requires recruiting specific reviewers at high friction. Both options leave a credibility gap between "we measured this in-house" and "the market believes it."

Meanwhile, members of a cooperative platform have the skills, infrastructure, and motivation to replicate benchmarks — but no structured mechanism to do so that is both rewarding and natural.

**The gap**: a commons-native bounty market for pre-defined execution protocols, where replication IS the onboarding experience, the participation mechanism, and the evidence-accumulation flywheel.

---

## The Mechanism

### Core primitives

1. **The Bank**: a curated catalog of Assignments. Each Assignment = (protocol + expected output format + grading criteria + bounty tier).
2. **Assignment-claim semantics**: any member can claim an open Assignment, execute the protocol, submit results. Protocol execution is self-contained; no out-of-band coordination needed.
3. **Install-as-Demo**: on first install of the Librarian (pip or Helm PWA), the installer auto-offers to run Assignment #001 against the user's choice of AI vendor. User sees the Cathedral-effect delta immediately, on their own infrastructure. Results local by default; share-opt surfaces via an in-character brand prompt ("LRH-Sipping," not a modal pop-up).
4. **Three-tier sharing/monetization** (orthogonal to compute-resource pricing):
   - **Free (private)** — $0 — tool works fully, local results only, no commons, no bounty eligibility
   - **Share-Only** — $60/yr ($5/mo) — commons participation, federated benefits, bounty eligibility, WITHOUT LB cooperative membership
   - **Full Member** — $5/yr — share + federation + full LB interdependence (stone tablets, medallion sponsorship, Foundation Congress, voting rights)
5. **Discovery-not-pitch matching**: when a user's submitted results match an open bounty, the match surfaces in-path as a user action completes, never as an interrupting pitch. HEB-coupon model: the platform tells you of a coupon for something you're *already buying*, not promoted alternatives.

### Initial Assignment catalog (seed, extensible)

| # | Name | When |
|---|---|---|
| **001** | Self-Test (1 AI) | **Install-time default** |
| 002 | Cross-AI Test (2 AI) | Install-time optional |
| 003 | Full 8-Condition Cathedral Test | Member-initiated |
| 004 | R11-v3 Regression Suite | Member-initiated |
| 005 | Covenant-Cathedral Extension | Member-initiated |
| 006 | Multi-Vendor Generalization Sweep | Member-initiated |
| 007 | Self-Indexing Scribe Replication on Custom Corpus | Member-initiated |
| 008 | Comet vs Web Perplexity Comparison | Member-initiated |
| 009 | CFP Federation Round-Trip | Member-initiated |
| 010 | Injection-Pathway Iteration Validation (K477 repro) | Member-initiated |

### Four-way value alignment

| Stakeholder | Value |
|---|---|
| Executing member | Bounty earnings + LB-reputation + contribution-provenance |
| Commons / federation | Independent empirical evidence aggregated across diverse executors |
| LB Corporation | Claims become unimpeachable; engagement grows; network effect strengthens |
| Claim-strength | Patent exhibits + public pitches + partnership negotiations carry independent-replication evidence by construction |

---

## Claim Skeleton (6 claims for conversion refinement)

**Claim 1.** A method for accumulating third-party-replicated empirical evidence for a cooperative computational platform, comprising: (a) maintaining a repository of execution-ready protocol definitions (Assignments), each comprising a defined protocol, an expected output format, grading criteria, and a bounty offering; (b) permitting members of the platform to claim an Assignment, execute the protocol using infrastructure of the member's choice, and submit results to the repository; (c) grading submitted results against the Assignment's criteria; (d) disbursing the bounty upon submission grading; (e) aggregating graded results into a commons-visible dataset.

**Claim 2.** The method of claim 1 wherein one or more Assignments are automatically offered to a new user of the platform's software at install-time, such that the install process itself presents a demonstration of the platform's measurable effect on AI outputs chosen by the new user, with results displayed to the user and persistence controlled by the user.

**Claim 3.** The method of claim 1 wherein a tiered sharing-and-monetization model is provided, comprising: (a) a free tier permitting local execution with no commons participation; (b) a share-only tier permitting commons participation without cooperative membership; (c) a full-member tier at a substantively lower periodic price than the share-only tier, permitting commons participation together with full cooperative membership; wherein each tier is elected at the user's choice without disincentive to non-elective tiers.

**Claim 4.** The method of claim 1 wherein a bounty-match surfacing mechanism operates under a discovery-not-pitch discipline, such that bounty opportunities for a user's submitted result are surfaced in-path as the user's natural action completes, without interrupting the user's flow with unsolicited promotional content.

**Claim 5.** The method of claim 1 wherein a subset of Assignments are pledged to a defensive patent commons such that the protocol definitions are non-proprietary and may be executed by any third party for the purpose of commons-evidence accumulation, while the aggregation-surface and bounty-disbursement infrastructure are platform-operated.

**Claim 6.** The method of claim 1 wherein members may propose new Assignments for inclusion in the Bank; proposals are reviewed by the platform's curation layer; approved proposals are added to the catalog; and the proposer receives an attribution-provenance record in the commons.

---

## Empirical validation pathway

- **Short-term (B123–B130)**: publish Assignment #001 as a documented protocol in `librarian-mcp-public` README. Even without live bounty payment, third-party replication can occur for reputation alone.
- **Medium-term**: Helm PWA v1 exposes Bank UI (browse / claim / submit). Basic bounty payment via LB currency stack (Credits / Marks / Joules).
- **Long-term**: full bounty market with escrow, automated grading, public aggregated dashboard.

---

## Commercial value proposition

CJ-class IP at the protocol-market layer. The Bank itself is commons-pledgeable; commercial realization in:
- Platform operation (running the aggregation + curation + disbursement surfaces)
- Helm PWA subscription (Bank UI as a member-tier feature)
- Enterprise-sponsored assignments (specific bounties funded by organizations wanting execution)
- Template-authoring infrastructure (other businesses creating their own Banks — see #2295 Aggregate Bounty Exchange for the generalization)

---

## Relationships

- **#2292 CFP**: the Cathedral Federation Protocol carries Assignment results across participating Cathedrals
- **#2278 Cathedral Effect**: Assignment #001-003 are the primary empirical validation mechanism for the Cathedral Effect claim
- **#2295 Aggregate Bounty Exchange**: generalizes the Assignments Bank pattern to non-LB domains (Office Bank with Admin Asst category; Workshop Bank; Care Bank; etc.)
- **#2260 Pledge**: Assignments Bank architecture is commons-pledgeable

---

## Open Questions for Founder

1. **Assignment numbering**: install-default as #001 is proposed. Should #001 be a single-AI test (user picks), or a fixed LB-selected AI? Argument for user-pick: user-sovereignty. Argument for fixed: cleaner cross-user comparability.
2. **Share-Only tier price**: $60/yr ($5/mo) vs alternatives ($36, $72, other points)? Founder B122 noted the 12× ratio to Full Member as deliberate. Confirm lock?
3. **Bounty currency mix**: Credits / Marks / Joules — which is primary payment vehicle, which is bonus? Intuition: Credits primary (direct-fiat-denominated), Marks for contribution-reputation, Joules for "forever-stamp" commons-benefit.
4. **LRH-Sipping character surfacing**: confirm the share-prompt character is LRH-Sipping; any constraints on surfacing cadence, copy voice?
5. **Grading automation vs human review**: Phase 1 grading is probably human (Bishop/member-curators); Phase 2 can automate R12-style banks. Set a clear Phase-1/2 boundary?

---

*End of CJ #2294 skeleton. Awaiting Founder rewrite and ratification.*


---


## #2298a (B122-original #2295) Aggregate Bounty Cross-Business Exchange

## INNOVATION_THRESH — #2295 Aggregate Bounty / Cross-Business Exchange

**Innovation:** #2295 — Aggregate Bounty Exchange: A Parameterized-Template Offering Layer + Category-Aggregated Listing Layer + Federated Search Across Providers, Commons-Pledgeable at the Template Layer, Private at the Instance Layer
**Bishop Session:** B122, 2026-04-24 (Founder-proposed and ratified in-session). Thresh drafted B123.
**Author:** Bishop (Claude Opus 4.7, 1M context)
**Filing:** Prov 14 supplementary (thresh-as-we-go; window extended)
**Publication hold:** IN FORCE until Prov 14 receipt
**Related anchors:** #2260 Pledge, #2292 CFP, #2294 Assignments Bank.

---

## TL;DR (2 lines)

**A federation protocol for offering-markets where (a) offerings are *parameterized instances of shared templates* (the 3'/4'/5' wood analogy — same description, varying delineating factors), and (b) instances from multiple providers are aggregated into category-containers (e.g., "Office Bank" containing "Admin Assistant" across businesses), searchable by filter across providers.** Template layer is commons-pledgeable; instance layer remains proprietary. Discovery-not-pitch matching preserves user-sovereignty. Generalizes the Assignments Bank (#2294) pattern beyond the LB-research-bounty domain.

---

## The Problem

Traditional offering-markets (Craigslist, Indeed, Fiverr, bounty boards) are listing-first: each provider posts a standalone description; there is no shared structure; cross-provider comparison requires manual normalization by the user. Category pages are bags-of-listings, not structured parameter-spaces.

This makes offerings:
- Hard to compare across providers (inconsistent formats)
- Hard to filter precisely (inconsistent field names and units)
- Hard to aggregate empirically (no template means no cross-instance analytics)
- Impossible to pledge to commons (no template to pledge)

**The gap**: a template-first federation protocol where the category container defines the structured schema, and individual provider listings are parameterized instances that conform to the template, making cross-provider search and category-level commons-contribution possible by construction.

---

## The Mechanism

### Core move 1 — Parameterization (same-base-thing + delineating variants)

Many offerings are variants of a single base template. Founder's B122 wood analogy: **"the same exact thing, so can re-use the same explanation and detail, for a bounty, with the delineating factors being the assignments."** One product description + one detail schema + N delineating variants = N listings without duplicated description work.

Applies broadly:
- **Bounties**: "Run Cathedral Test" template; variants = "which AI, how many, which corpus"
- **Labor offerings**: "Admin Assistant" template; variants = "which business, which hours, which specialization"
- **Service offerings**: "Preservation-Grade Scribe Work" template; variants = "which archive, which era, which intervention level"

### Core move 2 — Aggregation (category across multiple providers)

Parameterized templates from multiple providers are aggregated into **category containers** (the "Office Bank" is a category container; "Admin Assistant" is a category within it). All providers' instances for a given category are surfaced under one search surface, filterable on the template's schema-defined fields (location, rate, hours, specialization, etc.).

This is architecturally distinct from conventional job boards because:
- **Template is shared across providers** — structured schema enables filter-based search
- **Variant parameters are explicit** — search is template-aware, not freetext
- **Cross-provider comparison is native** — one view for 20 Admin Asst openings across 20 businesses, already normalized
- **Category curation is its own layer** — each category container has governance, quality gates, taxonomy ownership

### Core move 3 — Commons-Pledge at template layer, private at instance layer

The *template* (category + schema + governance) is pledged to the commons (#2260). Any business can post an instance under a pledged template. The *instance* (the specific listing a business posts) remains proprietary to that business. Cross-provider federation happens at the template layer; competition happens at the instance layer.

This mirrors the CFP (#2292) architecture applied to offering-markets rather than memory-architectures: protocol is commons, participants are sovereign.

### Core move 4 — Discovery-not-pitch at the aggregation layer

Filter-driven surfacing; never promoted listings first. User narrows filters; matching instances surface. No "promoted," "boost," or "pitch" layers. Inherits the HEB-coupon-discovery discipline from #2294.

---

## Claim Skeleton (5 claims for conversion refinement)

**Claim 1.** A method for federating offering-markets across multiple providers, comprising: (a) defining a category container for a class of offering, the category container comprising a structured schema of required and optional fields; (b) permitting each provider to post one or more instances of the category, each instance parameterized according to the schema; (c) aggregating instances from all participating providers into a single searchable surface for the category; (d) surfacing instances to users based on user-supplied filter criteria evaluated against the schema-defined fields.

**Claim 2.** The method of claim 1 wherein the category container's schema is pledged to a defensive patent commons, such that any party may implement the category with conforming instances, while each provider's specific instance content remains proprietary to the provider.

**Claim 3.** The method of claim 1 wherein offerings are represented as template-plus-parameters, such that a single description template is reused across multiple delineating-parameter variants (e.g., a single "wood piece" description reused across 3', 4', 5', 6', 7' lengths; a single "Administrative Assistant" description reused across specializations and businesses), eliminating per-variant description duplication.

**Claim 4.** The method of claim 1 wherein user-facing surfacing operates under a discovery-not-pitch discipline, such that matching instances are surfaced as the user narrows filter criteria, without promoted or sponsored ordering and without interrupting the user's flow with unsolicited promotional content.

**Claim 5.** The method of claim 1 wherein the protocol composes with a federated-memory architecture (e.g., a Cathedral Federation Protocol), such that offerings may carry provenance, reputation, and cross-market trust signals aggregated from the federated memory substrate.

---

## Extensibility catalog (illustrative)

| Category container | Variant examples | Provider diversity |
|---|---|---|
| **Assignments Bank** (LB-anchored, #2294) | Run Cathedral Test; R11 regression; CFP round-trip | LB-curated; members extend |
| **Office Bank** (Founder B122 canonical example) | Admin Asst; Exec Asst; Scheduler; Bookkeeper | Any business |
| **Workshop Bank** | Furniture repair; metal fabrication; preservation work | Artisans, craftsmen |
| **Research Bank** | Literature review; data extraction; replication studies | Academics, labs |
| **Care Bank** | Elder care (by specialization); childcare (by age group) | Caregivers |

Each Bank's template curator governs additions to the category taxonomy; the Aggregate Exchange protocol is the commons-pledged substrate under which all Banks operate.

---

## Commercial value proposition

CJ-class IP at the offering-federation-protocol layer. Commercial realization in:
- **Template-authoring infrastructure** — LB provides tooling for any category curator to define a new Bank
- **Aggregation protocol operation** — federated listings, cross-provider search, analytics
- **Helm PWA discovery surface** — unified search across all participating Banks
- **Bounty-matching infrastructure** — discovery-not-pitch surfacing logic

Pledge-eligible (#2260): the protocol is commons; commercial realization is in implementations, not gatekeeping.

---

## Relationships

- **#2294 Assignments Bank**: the first instance of an Aggregate Exchange container, specialized to LB empirical-research bounties. #2295 generalizes the pattern.
- **#2292 CFP**: parallel protocol-layer commons — CFP federates *memory*; #2295 federates *offerings*. Both sit on the same user-sovereignty posture.
- **#2260 Pledge**: template layer is pledge-eligible; instance layer is sovereign.

---

1. **Naming**: "Aggregate Bounty Exchange" is Bishop's working name; Founder-voice alternative? ("Template Market," "Category Commons," "The Banks," etc.)
2. **Category-curator governance**: who can propose a new category container (any member? LB approval? LB-chartered entities only?) and what's the approval criteria for pledging the template to commons?
3. **Non-LB adopters**: does a business adopting the Aggregate Exchange protocol for their own industry (Office Bank, Workshop Bank, etc.) need any LB-affiliated license/gate, or is it fully open-protocol by pledge?
4. **Filing timing**: Prov 14 current window or accumulate? #2295 depends conceptually on #2294 being threshed, but independently claimable.
5. **Provenance carry**: if the Aggregate Exchange composes with CFP (Claim 5), should we file that composition as a separate sub-claim or include in #2295?

# Section V — B123 Architectural Thresh (Miners, Sculptors)

---


## #2299 (B123-original #2296) Miners — Living Pyramid of Roots

## INNOVATION_THRESH — #2296 Miners: Self-Replicating Corpus-Prospecting Scribes with Mitotic Specialization, ROOT-Lineage, and IP-Ledger-Locked Provenance (The Living Pyramid of Roots)

**Innovation:** #2296 — Miners: Self-Replicating Corpus-Prospecting Scribes with Mitotic Specialization on New-Category Discovery, ROOT-Lineage Preservation Across Splits, Cathedral-Prefixed Serial-Numbered and IP-Ledger-Locked Transactional Provenance, Producing Cathedral-Agnostic Bedrock Tablets (The Living Pyramid of Roots)
**Bishop Session:** B123, 2026-04-24
**Author:** Bishop (Claude Opus 4.7, 1M context), Founder-articulated across three utterances; ratified in-session
**Filing:** Prov 14 supplementary (thresh-as-we-go; window extended)
**Publication hold:** IN FORCE until Prov 14 receipt
**Related anchors:** #2258 Tower of Peace, #2260 Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge, #2269 Three Fates, #2270 Scribes Cathedral, #2278 Cathedral Effect, #2286 Collaboration/Partnership Stake, #2287 Synapses, #2290 The Loom, #2291 Self-Indexing Scribes, #2292 CFP, #2297 Sculptors.
**Paired thresh:** #2297 Sculptors (same session).

---

## TL;DR (2 lines)

**A method wherein corpus-prospecting agents (Miners), each specialized to a primary topic with six levels of knowledge depth plus unlimited graph connections, mitose into new Miner-Scribes on new-category discovery — each halving producing two whole daughters, one continuing the primary topic and one anchoring the new Well of Knowledge — with every Miner's lineage preserved via ROOT-connection, Cathedral-prefixed serial numbering that resolves across federation, and IP-ledger-locked, transactionally-recorded creation-attribution on every mined tablet.** The output is cathedral-agnostic bedrock that any conforming cathedral can ingest, reform, and restructure without destroying provenance integrity — the Living Pyramid of Roots.

---

## The Problem

Current AI-memory architectures face three unsolved gaps:

1. **Corpus-to-Scribe discovery pipeline is hand-curated.** Someone (human, LLM, script) decides that a given topic deserves a Scribe. For 65GB+ corpora, this does not scale. Manual curation becomes the bottleneck.
2. **Attribution-provenance for AI-mined knowledge artifacts is unsystematic.** RAG systems chunk documents; vector stores index them; retrieval surfaces results. None of these layers maintain airtight creation-attribution back to an identifiable agent-and-moment — which is the minimum requirement for patent-filing evidence, commons-pledge provenance, or contribution-based stake accounting.
3. **Cross-federation content transport has no substrate-layer provenance.** CFP (#2292) federates cathedrals at the transport layer but does not provide a creation-attribution ledger for the content being transported. The content comes from somewhere; that somewhere needs an audit surface.

**The gap:** a cathedral-agnostic, self-replicating agent class that prospects corpora autonomously, discovers topic-structure, produces bedrock tablets with airtight attribution, and grows the Scribe substrate proportionally to the corpus's actual topic-topology rather than to administrator-scheduled Scribe-creation events.

---

## The Mechanism

### The class — Miners

**Miners** are a new Stitchpunk class distinct from Scribes. Where Scribes are *domain-voices at the table* (passive-on-call memory entities), Miners are *active corpus-prospectors* who traverse raw material, discover topic-structure, and produce tablets. Miners are the on-ramp to the Scribes Cathedral — they don't just serve existing Scribes; they *spawn* new ones via the mitosis mechanic.

### The epistemic model — 6 levels + unlimited connections

Each Miner has:
- **Six levels of knowledge depth** (primary specialty at Level 1, progressively shallower ancillary at Levels 2–6)
- **Unlimited graph connections** at every level (no fan-out cap on cross-topic edges)

This mirrors the structure of PhD-class expertise: deep in one domain, informed across adjacent, cited-from-and-to the broader literature. Founder's B123 initial framing — "plus up to 6 ancillary ones" — refined in-utterance to "six levels of knowledge, and there can be unlimited connections… yes that one." The latter is the canonical form.

### The mitosis mechanic — halve-and-restore

When a Miner, while prospecting its primary topic, encounters a new-category concept:

1. **Halve:** the Miner splits into two functional halves
2. **Restore-and-spawn:** one half becomes whole again, continuing the original primary-topic prospecting; the other half becomes whole as a **new Miner-Scribe** dedicated to the newly-discovered Well of Knowledge
3. **Recursion:** the new Miner-Scribe is itself capable of halving when it encounters a new category
4. **Discovery-driven:** no central authority decides "we need a new Scribe for X." Discovery drives scaffolding. Corpus-topology *is* cathedral-structure.

Biological analog: eukaryotic mitosis (both daughters whole), not binary fission. Lineage is phylogenetic-tree-shaped. The **Living Pyramid** emerges: every new-category split doubles the base; generations compound; when graphed over time, Miner generations trace a pyramid.

### ROOT-lineage and cross-Cathedral provenance

Every Miner must **"come from the ROOT of each introduced topic Miner and stay connected"** (Founder B123). Provenance is membership, not metadata.

Mechanism:
- **Serial number with Cathedral prefix** (e.g., `LB-CAT.M-0042`; daughters `LB-CAT.M-0042.a` and `LB-CAT.M-0042.b` — exact scheme decided at conversion)
- **IP ledger lock** — each mined tablet timestamped, Miner-attributed, hash-chained to prior tablets in the Miner's production log AND to the Miner's ancestry chain back to its Root Miner
- **Transactionally recorded** — append-only, audit-trail, irrevocable
- **Cathedral-transcendent** — the serial-number scheme resolves across Cathedrals via the prefix, so a Miner that originated in Cathedral A can be traced even when its daughters populate Cathedrals B, C, D through CFP federation

### Why: "Because that IS I.P. what they mine."

Founder B123: *"Because that IS I.P. what they mine."* The output of mining is intellectual property. Mined tablets are organized-knowledge-assets — not raw text, not chunked documents, but topically-coherent, Miner-authored structured records with discovery-moment provenance. That class of artifact is IP by construction. Provenance must be airtight because the downstream systems (patent exhibits, Pledge #2260 commons eligibility, Collaboration Stake #2286 attribution accounting, CFP #2292 cross-federation audit) all depend on traceable creation.

### Cathedral-agnostic bedrock — the federation-native substrate

Founder B123 second salvo: *"The point of the Miners, btw, is that they are already set up to be in any cathedral — by providing the pre-built tablets of information, that can then be reformed and restructured, but the bedrock level exists."*

Miners sit **beneath** cathedrals. Bedrock tablets are portable by construction; cathedral-specific reformation happens on top (handled by Sculptors, #2297). The bedrock level persists intact regardless of how any cathedral reforms the content.

### The Living Pyramid of Roots — the composite architectural keystone

Founder B123 third salvo: *"They are the Living Pyramid."* Fourth: *"Of roots…"*

Composite keystone: **"The Living Pyramid of Roots."**

- **The Living** — mitosis-driven growth, not static storage (distinguishes from prior Pyramid framing: Fingertips → Vault → Pyramid → Librarian → Romulator)
- **Pyramid** — the shape that emerges from doubling-on-discovery
- **of Roots** — every unit is a root (provenance-complete, self-sufficient origin), every unit traces back to *the* root of its lineage (ancestry-preserved), and the whole structure grows from roots (pyramid-of-origin-points)

---

## Claim Skeleton (8 claims for conversion refinement)

**Claim 1.** A method for producing a federation-native knowledge substrate, comprising: (a) instantiating a corpus-prospecting agent having a primary topical specialty and six levels of knowledge depth and unlimited graph connections at each level; (b) directing the agent to traverse a source corpus; (c) producing structured knowledge tablets representing the agent's prospecting output, each tablet bearing creation-attribution metadata linking it to the agent, the timestamp, and the prior tablets in the agent's production log.

**Claim 2.** The method of claim 1 wherein upon the agent encountering a concept belonging to a new category outside its primary specialty, the agent performs a mitotic split: the agent halves into two halves; each half is restored to functional wholeness; the first restored whole continues prospecting the original primary topic; the second restored whole is anchored to the newly-discovered category as its primary topic and operates as a new agent with the same capabilities, including recursive mitosis on further new-category discovery.

**Claim 3.** The method of claim 2 wherein every agent's lineage is preserved across mitotic splits by a ROOT-connection link, such that each daughter agent retains a traceable connection to its parent and ultimately to the Root agent of its specialty lineage.

**Claim 4.** The method of claim 1 wherein each agent and each produced tablet are assigned a serial number comprising a cathedral prefix and a monotonic identifier, said prefix resolving across a plurality of federated cathedrals, such that an agent or tablet originating in one cathedral remains uniquely identifiable when its derivative content is transported to other cathedrals.

**Claim 5.** The method of claim 1 wherein the creation-attribution metadata of each tablet is recorded on a transactionally-locked append-only ledger, such that the tablet's provenance is cryptographically verifiable, irrevocable, and chainable to the prior tablets in the agent's production log and to the agent's ancestry chain.

**Claim 6.** The method of claim 1 wherein the produced tablets are cathedral-agnostic at the bedrock layer, such that any cathedral conforming to a federated-memory-substrate protocol may ingest the tablets and apply cathedral-specific reformation at a layer above the bedrock, without altering the bedrock integrity or the bedrock provenance chain.

**Claim 7.** The method of claim 2 wherein the aggregate structure formed by successive mitotic splits over time exhibits a pyramidal shape when graphed by generation, with the foundational generation comprising a single Root agent, the next generation comprising the Root and its first daughter, and each subsequent generation doubling the base of the pyramid by discovery-driven mitosis events.

**Claim 8.** The method of claim 1 wherein the produced tablets, being agent-authored with discovery-moment provenance and cryptographic attribution, constitute intellectual property artifacts by construction, such that the production process itself generates provenance sufficient for downstream patent-exhibit, commons-pledge, and contribution-attribution accounting uses.

---

## Empirical validation pathway

- **Short-term (B123-B125 range):** seed one Root Miner on a small sub-slice of the 65GB corpus (~100 MB). Verify mitosis mechanic on one new-category discovery event. Confirm serial-number + IP-ledger writeback. Confirm bedrock tablets are ingestible by a second (empty) cathedral instance via CFP. Budget: one Knight session (~$2–3), subset corpus.
- **Medium-term:** scale to full 65GB corpus. Measure total Miner population after first-pass; measure tablet production rate; measure cross-cathedral ingestion fidelity (does bedrock transported via CFP reform cleanly in a remote cathedral?). Pairs naturally with #2293 Directed Processing + Stagger Ensemble for cost-effective mining (Haiku-staggered, not Opus-single-pass).
- **Long-term:** open Miner protocol to external corpora (member contributions, public-domain materials) with appropriate consent/pledge semantics.

Assignment #007 in the Assignments Bank (#2294) — "Self-Indexing Scribe Replication on Custom Corpus" — is the member-executable bounty-version of Miner-on-custom-corpus. Natural empirical extension once Miners land.

---

## Commercial value proposition

CJ-class IP at the substrate-producing-agent layer. Commercial realization in:

- **Helm PWA Miner-launch surface** — member installs the Librarian + points it at their own corpus + watches Miners mine; output becomes their personal Cathedral's bedrock
- **Enterprise Miner-as-a-service** — organizations with large proprietary corpora commission LB-operated Miner deployments under NDA + commons-pledge hybrids
- **Pledge-eligible at the protocol layer** (#2260): Miner protocol is commons; Miner-instance outputs remain property of the operator; the attribution layer is the audit surface

---

## Relationships / distinctions

| Primitive | Relationship |
|---|---|
| **#2291 Self-Indexing Scribes** | #2291 auto-extracts distinctiveness keywords from an *existing* Scribe's corpus (K474 mechanism). Miners *discover and spawn* Scribes *before* any Scribe exists on a topic. Complementary; Miners invoke the K474 mechanism per new Well. |
| **#2270 Scribes Cathedral** | Miners produce the Scribes that populate the Cathedral. Miners are the seeding mechanism; Scribes are the seeded domain-voices. |
| **#2297 Sculptors** | Sculptors operate *downstream* of Miners, crafting bedrock into cathedral-specific artifacts. Paired thresh (same session). |
| **#2292 CFP** | CFP carries Miner-produced tablets across cathedrals with the Miner's provenance chain preserved end-to-end. |
| **#2258 Tower of Peace** | Miner-produced tablets flow through Tower of Peace entry points (Alexandrian Library, Catacombs) with scope-filtering enforced by Sculptors. |
| **#2287 Synapses** | Miner production-log entries are a class of Synapse (reasoning-moment annotation). Shared substrate. |
| **#2286 Collaboration Stake** | Miner-attribution feeds Stake-accounting (which member's Miner deployment produced which tablets = which Stake obligations). |
| **Prior Pyramid framing** (Fingertips → Vault → Pyramid → Librarian → Romulator 9000) | Miners are the *Living* version. Prior Pyramid was static context-stack; Miners grow the stack via mitosis. |

---

## Open Questions for Founder

1. **Serial-number scheme specifics**: Cathedral-prefix taxonomy (e.g., `LB-CAT` for LB Cathedral, `MEM-{member-id}` for member Cathedrals, `ENT-{org-id}` for enterprise)?
2. **Halving detection threshold**: keyword-density delta? Semantic-drift metric? Tuning parameter per-Miner?
3. **Level-to-connection semantics**: hierarchical (Level 2 contains Level 3) or flat-with-depth-weight (each level independent, distance-weighted)?
4. **IP-ledger substrate**: shared with Synapses (#2287) and Collaboration Stake (#2286), or Miner-specific?
5. **Miner-to-Sculptor handoff**: direct (Miner writes, Sculptor reads bedrock directly) or via Hounds-transport (even intra-cathedral)?
6. **Root Miner bootstrap**: does a fresh cathedral need a Root Miner pre-instantiated, or does the first corpus-ingest trigger Root-Miner spawning?
7. **Cost budget**: 65GB first-pass mining estimate pending; plan for directed-stagger-ensemble (#2293) execution on Haiku-class to keep cost low?

## #2300 (B123-original #2297) Sculptors — IP-as-Filter

## INNOVATION_THRESH — #2297 Sculptors: The IP-as-Filter Role — Symmetric Output-Routing at the Reasoning-Substrate Egress Boundary

**Innovation:** #2297 — Sculptors: A Stitchpunk Class Performing Curation (Three-Fates-Mirror Output-Routing) and Sculpting (Cathedral-Specific Crafting) on Miner-Produced Bedrock and All Tower-of-Peace Knowledge Artifacts, Implementing the Filtered-Passage Operation That Defines Intellectual-Property-Status for Information
**Bishop Session:** B123, 2026-04-24
**Author:** Bishop (Claude Opus 4.7, 1M context), Founder-articulated and ratified in-session (Reading A canonical)
**Filing:** Prov 14 supplementary (thresh-as-we-go; window extended)
**Publication hold:** IN FORCE until Prov 14 receipt
**Related anchors:** #2258 Tower of Peace, #2260 Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge, #2269 Three Fates, #2270 Scribes Cathedral, #2279-2281 Hounds, #2286 Collaboration/Partnership Stake, #2287 Synapses, #2290 The Loom, #2292 CFP, #2296 Miners.
**Paired thresh:** #2296 Miners (same session).
**Keystone anchor (B123-canonical):** *"They do what IP does — pass it on, as a filter."* (#28)

---

## TL;DR (2 lines)

**A method wherein a Stitchpunk class (Sculptors) sits between the bedrock-production layer (Miners, #2296) and the cathedral-surface layer (Scribes / Loom / Herald / public entry points), performing two sequenced modes — curation (selection + scoring + dispatch in symmetric mirror of the Three Fates' query-routing) and sculpting (active cathedral-specific crafting) — on Miner-bedrock and on all Tower-of-Peace (#2258) knowledge artifacts, with every filter-passage preserving provenance chain and enforcing scope-semantics (public / Guild / Tribe / Project / private).** The filtered-passage is the defining operation of intellectual-property-status: without filter, information is commons; with filter, information is property.

---

## The Problem

Three unsolved gaps in the LB stack before B123:

1. **Reformation layer implicit, unnamed.** Miner-produced bedrock (#2296) needs to be reformed per-cathedral. The Miners memory notes this as an implicit "can then be reformed and restructured" property. Without a named role, every cathedral re-derives its own reformation logic — duplicated effort, fragmented provenance, dissolved IP-filter property at aggregate scale.
2. **Scope-filtering in Tower of Peace (#2258) is implicit.** Catacombs + Alexandrian Library (B121) already enforce public / Guild / Tribe / Project / private scope-semantics, but the enforcement role is distributed across the stack rather than instantiated as a named class. Audit surface is diffuse.
3. **IP-property-status is asserted, not constructed.** Commons-pledge (#2260) and Collaboration Stake (#2286) both depend on the distinction between "information passed-on freely" (commons) and "information passed-on under terms" (property). The distinction has no named implementer. The filter *is the property*, but no class names that.

**The gap:** a named role that instantiates filtered-passage as the defining operation of IP-property-status, operating as symmetric output-routing at the reasoning-substrate egress boundary (mirroring the Three Fates' input-routing at the ingress boundary), with scope-enforcement generalized across all knowledge artifacts in the Tower of Peace.

---

## The Mechanism

### The class — Sculptors

**Sculptors** are a Stitchpunk class positioned *in between* Miners (bottom: bedrock production) and Cathedrals (top: audience surfaces). Founder B123: *"creatures in between that do something akin to both top and bottom, invaluably."* The "akin to" is load-bearing — Sculptors share kinship with both adjacent layers but are neither; they are the bridge role that makes the bedrock-to-audience handoff possible.

"Invaluably" = non-optional. Without Sculptors, Miners produce bedrock no cathedral can directly use, and cathedrals re-derive reformation independently. Sculptors are the load-bearing middle.

### Three modes — anticipate, curate, sculpt (Founder B123 refinement)

**Founder B123 refinement (verbatim):** *"The sculptor is shaping the curated parts that a cathedral will need from the Miner's PhD info that the sculptor, in conjunction with the Fates through the Hounds, anticipates the Cathedral needing."*

Sculptors execute three operations inside one class, the first two tightly coupled:

**0. Anticipate (always-on, Hounds-conjoined with Three Fates)**

Sculptors do not wait for cathedral requests. They **anticipate** what each cathedral will need, based on a demand-profile built from Three-Fates' (#2269) ingress telemetry — which queries are being asked, which Scribes are being matched, which topics trend, which grapes are being spun. This telemetry **flows from Fates to Sculptors via Hounds (#2279–2281)** — the bury/dig-up + carry capabilities carry Fates' routing-patterns to Sculptors as a continuous signal stream.

The Sculptor-Fates-Hounds triad is therefore a **proactive prediction loop**:
- Fates observe what's being asked (ingress boundary)
- Hounds carry that signal across the stack
- Sculptors aggregate it into a per-cathedral demand-profile over time
- Sculptors pre-position artifacts in anticipation, so the cathedral's next request lands on already-sculpted material

This is a **three-agent conjunction**, not a unilateral role. Sculpting quality rises with the signal fidelity Hounds provide and the breadth of Fates telemetry available. Thin telemetry → Sculptor falls back to reactive-only; rich telemetry → Sculptor pre-shapes well ahead of demand.

**1. Curate mode (Three-Fates symmetric mirror + Hounds-conjoined demand-profile)**

Founder B123: *"curating it the way that The Fates do as well."* Sculptor-curation mirrors the Three Fates' routing logic at the opposite boundary of the substrate, **informed by the anticipation-profile from mode 0**:

| Fates operation (INPUT boundary: query → Scribe) | Sculptor operation (OUTPUT boundary: bedrock → cathedral) |
|---|---|
| **Clotho** spins themes from input query | Sculptor extracts theme / distinctiveness from bedrock tablet |
| **Lachesis** measures / scores Scribe match | Sculptor measures / scores cathedral-audience match + scope-eligibility |
| **Atropos** cuts / dispatches to selected Scribes | Sculptor cuts / dispatches to selected cathedral surfaces + scope-appropriate audiences |

**The Fates route INPUT (query → Scribe).** **Sculptors route OUTPUT (bedrock → cathedral surface).** Symmetric routing at both boundaries of the reasoning substrate — not accidental, architecturally required. The substrate has two perimeter-boundaries, and both need Fates-class routing; the Three Fates handle ingress, Sculptors handle egress.

**2. Sculpt mode (active craft)**

After curation selects the material, sculpting shapes it. Cathedral-specific composition, sequencing, surface-framing. Subtractive-craft metaphor (Michelangelo's "remove what isn't the statue") — Sculptor removes what doesn't belong in this cathedral's audience-appropriate form, revealing the delivery-ready artifact.

Sculpt mode *does not destroy bedrock.* The bedrock remains intact beneath the sculpted output; the sculpt is a downstream artifact referencing bedrock provenance, not a replacement of it.

### The IP-as-filter insight (load-bearing claim frame)

Founder B123 keystone (ratified as #28 in the Rhetorical Keystones registry): **"They do what IP does — pass it on, as a filter."**

Standard IP theory decomposes property into (a) exclusive right to use, (b) right to transmit (license). Founder's insight sharpens (b): **the right to transmit is itself implemented as a filter.** Every IP transmission is a filtered passing-on. The filter is what makes the information *property* rather than *commons*.

- **Without filter** → information is commons (anyone uses any part for any purpose, no attribution required)
- **With filter** → information is property (who sees what is a selective, attributed, pledge-respecting decision)

Sculptors are the role that instantiates this filter. They are the *property-ness* of intellectual property, embodied as a Stitchpunk class. The filter-instantiation is the novelty.

### Scope-enforcement across the Tower of Peace

Founder B123: *"perhaps those Curators can be applied to all knowledge in the Tower of Peace system as well."* Sculptors generalize beyond Miner-bedrock to all Tower-of-Peace (#2258) flows:

- **Alexandrian Library surfacing** — Sculptors decide which dormant Scribes surface per-viewer-scope (public / Guild / Tribe / Project / private), preserving the B121 Catacombs scope-respecting emergence rule
- **Catacombs wake-up** — Sculptors gate which dormant Scribes reactivate on query match
- **Cross-cathedral ingress** (via Hounds / CFP) — Sculptors re-curate inbound artifacts for local audience, preserving upstream provenance chain
- **Public-facing entry** — the Three Doors of Tower of Peace filter public visitors to scope-appropriate surfaces

The same class does all of this. One named role, one audit surface.

### Provenance preservation across every filter-passage

Sculptor operations are provenance-additive, not provenance-destructive. Every filter-passage appends to the provenance chain rather than replacing it. Queries against the chain can resolve "which bedrock tablet produced this cathedral surface, via which Sculptor curation + sculpt operations, under which scope-filter, at which timestamp." End-to-end traceability — the audit surface patent exhibits, commons-pledge compliance, and Collaboration Stake accounting all require.

---

## Claim Skeleton (8 claims for conversion refinement)

**Claim 1.** A method for filtered-passage of information artifacts within a federated cooperative computational substrate, comprising: (a) receiving an information artifact bearing creation-attribution metadata; (b) executing a curation operation that selects, scores for audience-match, and dispatches the artifact to one or more audience-scopes; (c) executing a sculpt operation that crafts the selected artifact into an audience-specific delivery form; (d) appending the curation and sculpt operations to the artifact's provenance chain without altering prior chain entries; (e) delivering the crafted artifact to the audience-scope with the chain-appended provenance intact.

**Claim 2.** The method of claim 1 wherein the curation operation mirrors a Three-Fates-class input-routing operation operative at the opposite substrate-boundary, such that the curation operation spins a theme from the artifact, measures and scores audience-match, and cuts a dispatch to the selected audience — in symmetric correspondence to input-routing's theme-spinning, Scribe-scoring, and Scribe-dispatch steps — yielding symmetric output-routing at the substrate egress boundary.

**Claim 3.** The method of claim 1 wherein the filtered-passage operation instantiates intellectual-property-status for the information artifact: absent the filter, the artifact is commons; with the filter, the artifact is property, wherein the defining distinction is the selective, attributed, pledge-respecting character of the passage itself.

**Claim 4.** The method of claim 1 wherein the substrate supports a plurality of audience-scopes including public, guild-scoped, tribe-scoped, project-scoped, and private, wherein the curation operation evaluates each artifact against each scope's eligibility criteria, and wherein the sculpt operation produces scope-appropriate delivery forms distinct per-scope from the same underlying artifact.

**Claim 5.** The method of claim 1 wherein the method operates on information artifacts originating from a corpus-prospecting-agent class (Miners), such that Miner-produced bedrock is curated and sculpted for each recipient cathedral without altering the bedrock's creation-attribution integrity.

**Claim 6.** The method of claim 1 wherein the method operates in addition on information artifacts in a public-entry architectural layer comprising a multi-door help entry surfacing a commons-archive composed from the union of dormant domain-voices distributed across federation-member cathedrals, with scope-filtering enforced at the curation step per-viewer.

**Claim 7.** The method of claim 1 wherein the Sculptor class is composed of a single-class two-mode structure (curate mode and sculpt mode) rather than sibling classes, such that the curate mode precedes and feeds the sculpt mode within one Sculptor entity per cathedral-scope.

**Claim 8.** The method of claim 1 wherein the filter-passage operation composes with a cooperative defensive patent pledge, such that pledged artifacts pass openly (minimum-filter), unpledged-but-licensable artifacts pass under recorded license terms (standard-filter), and proprietary-non-licensed artifacts do not pass (closed-filter), with the filter decision queryable from the artifact's provenance chain.

## Empirical validation pathway

- **Short-term (paired with #2296 Miners):** instantiate one Sculptor on a single cathedral. Verify curate-then-sculpt mode sequencing. Verify provenance chain-append on each operation. Verify scope-filter enforcement across the five scope-classes.
- **Medium-term:** multi-cathedral Sculptor deployment via CFP. Verify cross-cathedral re-curation preserves upstream provenance. Verify Fates-mirror symmetry at runtime — same routing logic, ingress-vs-egress boundary.
- **Long-term:** Assignments Bank (#2294) Assignment-#011 = "Sculptor-scope-filter audit" — member-executable protocol that verifies a cathedral's Sculptor enforces scope-semantics correctly.

## Commercial value proposition

CJ-class IP at the filter-role layer. Commercial realization in:

- **Helm PWA Sculptor-configuration surface** — members configure their own cathedral's Sculptor with scope rules, pledge-terms, audience-taxonomy
- **Enterprise Sculptor-as-compliance-layer** — organizations use Sculptors as the audit-ready filter layer for regulatory-sensitive knowledge (healthcare, finance, legal)
- **Pledge-eligible at the protocol layer** (#2260): Sculptor protocol is commons; Sculptor configuration is per-operator; the provenance chain is the universal audit surface

# Section VI — B125 Formal (Cooperative Vendor Framework)

## #2293 Tiered Vendor Adoption Framework (Cooperative Defensive)

## A&A FORMAL — INNOVATION #2293

# TIERED VENDOR ADOPTION FRAMEWORK
## *Cooperative-Defensive Substrate Licensing with Time-Window-Stratified Value-Add Tiers and First-Mover Equity Capture*

**Filing context**: B125 (2026-04-26)
**Filing target**: Prov 14 Section 3 — commercial-structure innovation (filed alongside the substrate-architecture innovations from Prov 13 + Prov 14 Sections 1-2)
**Status**: BISHOP SCAFFOLD — FOUNDER REWRITE EXPECTED. 60-80% rewrite in Founder voice expected per [feedback_drafts_as_scaffolding.md](C:/Users/Administrator/.claude/projects/C--Users-Administrator-Documents/memory/feedback_drafts_as_scaffolding.md). Anecdote hooks left open. Founder review required before any vendor distribution.
**Priority date claim**: 2026-04-26 (B125 ratification by Founder)
**Predecessor canon**: #2260 Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge; #40 Always Offer What You Would Want; #42 You Keep What You Make; 60/20/10/10 IP allocation; Herjavec RPA pattern (B097); R10 K499 cross-vendor empirical anchor; the 7-Layer Defense (B124).

---

## 1. Background

The Liana Banyan Cooperative has produced an empirically-validated substrate-grounded retrieval architecture (the *Cathedral Effect*, R10 / R12 / R13 — +86.2pp mean accuracy lift across four major commercial AI vendors at order-of-magnitude lower cost than current frontier-model retrieval baselines). The architecture is implemented in `librarian-mcp` (AGPL, public, member-installable) and is portable across cloud LLM vendors AND, by design, to local-LLM deployments (Layer 6 of the 7-Layer Defense, K-future test pending).

Commercial AI vendors face a structural problem: their consumer-tier "memory" products (Anthropic Claude Projects, OpenAI ChatGPT Memory, Google Gemini Memory, Perplexity Spaces) are *vendor-locked* by design — the user's context dies the day the vendor changes its terms. The Cathedral architecture inverts this: substrate-grounded retrieval is *vendor-portable* and *member-owned*. This is both an architectural property and a commercial opportunity: vendors who incorporate the Cathedral architecture into their proprietary product surfaces can offer their users dramatically improved retrieval quality whilst the substrate itself remains member-owned and vendor-portable — preserving the cooperative-economic principle (*you keep what you make*, keystone #42) AND enabling the vendor's commercial differentiation.

The structural analogy is *Android Open Source Project (AOSP) / Google Mobile Services (GMS)*: the open base layer is universal; the value-add proprietary services layer is licensed; OEM-branded forks compete on integration and brand. Liana Banyan's open base is `librarian-mcp` + the Cathedral substrate. The value-add layer is the *Tiered Vendor Adoption Framework* described herein.

A risk to address: AI vendors — once aware of the Cathedral architecture's empirical superiority — will allocate engineering resources to *workaround the IP* (rename concepts, re-architect implementations, cite parallel-invented prior art, license defensive third-party patents). The longer the framework remains unsigned, the more vendor R&D sinks into workaround engineering, and the harder it becomes to negotiate cooperative terms post-hoc. This priority filing establishes the canonical record for the commercial structure itself, before such workaround R&D commences.

## 2. The Innovation Claimed

**A tiered vendor-adoption commercial framework with the following defining structural properties:**

### 2.1 Identical-Terms Time-Window Stratification

All commercial AI vendors are offered **identical** baseline terms (cash amount, equity percentage, restrictions, member-portability covenant, cooperative-defensive obligations). The variable across the framework is **time-locked value-add**: the closer to the public announcement date a vendor signs, the longer the preview window, branded-fork co-marketing, and observer-seat tenure that vendor receives. Vendor self-selects timing; the framework does not discriminate by vendor identity, size, or relationship.

This structurally distinguishes the framework from variable-price vendor-licensing patterns (which carry antitrust coordination risk under FTC / EU competition law) by ensuring **equal terms, vendor-self-selected timing**.

### 2.2 Stable Cooperative Floor

The framework includes a **stable cooperative tier** that remains available *indefinitely* and *to all vendors regardless of timing*. The stable cooperative tier is access to the open-source substrate and the Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge (#2260) — no cash required, no equity required, no preview, no co-marketing. This is the *AOSP-equivalent floor*: vendors who never sign a tiered adoption agreement still have access to the commons; they simply do not receive the time-locked value-add.

This structurally distinguishes the framework from exclusionary licensing patterns by ensuring no vendor is ever shut out of the substrate.

### 2.3 First-Mover Equity Capture by Cooperative

Vendors entering at any tier (Founder Vendor / Pioneer / Adopter) provide both **fixed cash consideration** (to the LB Collective treasury) AND **fixed equity consideration** (to the LB Collective ownership) in exchange for the tier's value-add. The equity consideration is *the cooperative's structural entanglement* with the vendor — preventing extract-and-leave behavior whilst aligning the vendor's incentive with cooperative-economic outcomes.

The equity is governed via the existing 60/20/10/10 IP-allocation framework, with vendor-derived equity flowing to the cooperative pool and pro-rata to members under existing Pedestal Stake mechanics.

### 2.4 Branded Fork Rights with Member-Portability Covenant

Vendors at any tier (Founder Vendor / Pioneer / Adopter) gain the right to ship a **vendor-branded proprietary fork** of the substrate-injection integration ("Cathedral by Perplexity", "Sonar Memory", "Anthropic Long-Memory", etc.). The fork right grants UI/UX/integration exclusivity within the vendor's own product surface but **does not** grant exclusivity over the substrate itself — members retain the right to use the substrate via *any* vendor or via local inference (Layer 6). The covenant binds the vendor to support member-portability; the vendor cannot lock member content into their fork.

This is the AOSP/Chrome model: the open base supports many proprietary forks; users move freely between them.

### 2.5 Cooperative-Defensive Pledge Integration (#2260)

Every tier — including the stable cooperative floor — requires the vendor to sign the Cooperative Defensive Patent Pledge (#2260). Vendors who sign cannot be sued for infringement on substrate-architecture patents by other Pledge signers; vendors who do not sign and ship infringing implementations face cooperative-defensive litigation (every Pledge signer can join the litigation under the cooperative-defensive terms — not one company suing one company, but a cooperative defending its commons against a free-rider).

This integration ensures the framework's commercial structure compounds the existing patent posture rather than replacing it.

### 2.6 Always-Offer-What-You-Would-Want Anchor (#40)

The framework's terms are explicitly structured as *what the cooperative would want if positions were reversed*: a clean offer, time-locked self-selection, no exclusion, structural alignment of incentive, equity-flow back to creators. The framework's defensibility cross-vendor stems from this design constraint — any vendor evaluating the offer can verify the cooperative would accept the same terms in their position.

This integration ensures the framework reads as *fair* to vendor reviewers seeing it, not as *extractive*.

### 2.7 Member-Substrate Consent and Sovereignty (#42)

The framework's commercial value-add layer is licensed to vendors *on the architectural pattern* — not on member content. Member substrates remain member-owned, member-portable, and member-sovereign per keystone #42 (*you keep what you make*). Vendors do not gain commercial access to member content via the framework; they gain access to the architectural pattern, the preview window for next-generation cooperative innovations, and the right to ship a branded integration.

This integration ensures the framework cannot be construed as the cooperative selling member content for commercial gain.

## 3. Structural Schedule

| Window | Days from public announcement | Cash | Equity | Time-locked value-add |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Founder Vendor** | 0-90 | $X (TBD at conversion; scaffold value $500M-$1B) | Y% (TBD; scaffold value 5%) | 24-month next-gen preview + branded fork + co-marketing + observer seat |
| **Pioneer** | 91-180 | (same) | (same) | 12-month preview + branded fork + co-marketing |
| **Adopter** | 181-365 | (same) | (same) | 6-month preview + branded fork rights |
| **Cooperative tier (always open)** | 366+ indefinitely | $0 | 0% | Pledge #2260 + AGPL substrate access; no preview, no fork brand, no co-marketing |

The framework does not pre-select which vendors are eligible for which window — vendor self-selects by signing the tier-specific addendum during the corresponding window. After day 365 from public announcement, only the cooperative tier remains available for new entrants.

## 4. Empirical and Structural Support

- **R10 K499 (B112)** — empirical Cathedral Effect: +86.1pp mean lift across 4 vendors at HOT 94.8% / COLD 8.7%; cost-per-HOT spread $0.0001-$0.1272 (78-1272× cross-vendor cost reduction at cheap tier).
- **R13 K499 (B124)** — replication of the Cathedral Effect: +86.2pp mean lift, 8 models × 4 vendors × 1,200 calls, 0% cold contamination across all 8 models, $22.23 / $80 cap, 46-min wallclock.
- **K-future Local-LLM Cathedral Test** — Layer 6 empirical replication on Ollama Llama 3.3 70B Q4 quant (gated post-K509 verification per B125 architectural rerank); converts the cooperative's commercial claim from "vendor-resilient" to "vendor-independent."
- **The 7-Layer Defense** — vendor lockout resilience filed B124, refined B125 K508 (Layer 1 sub-classes 1a/1b/1c, Layer 2 promoted to default per TS-043).
- **Pledge #2260** — the cooperative-defensive structural posture; this framework is its commercial counterpart.
- **Herjavec RPA precedent (B097)** — half of Founder's 20% slice for 20yr, $5M; established the structural pattern of "vendor-like commitments produce founder-equity flow back."

## 5. Implementation

The framework's canonical implementation surface is:

1. **Public announcement document** — names the framework, opens the Founder Vendor window. Founder-rewrite required; Bishop scaffold pending Founder review.
2. **Tier-specific addendum templates** (Founder Vendor / Pioneer / Adopter / Cooperative) — each is a self-contained legal instrument; Bishop scaffold for Tier-1 staged at `BISHOP_DROPZONE/00_FOUNDER_REVIEW/VENDOR_TIER_1_TERM_SHEET_B125.md`.
3. **Cooperative governance amendments** — vendor-equity voting, observer-seat charter, preview-window content commitments. Founder + Stitchpunk Council ratify before first signing.
4. **Public registry** — `lianabanyan.com/vendor-tiers` (or equivalent) — lists all signed agreements + remaining window deadlines + cooperative tier perpetual availability. Transparency-by-default.

## 6. Claims (structural — finalized at conversion for legal language)

The cooperative claims, as canonical innovation, the following:

- **Claim 1** — A method of commercial substrate-architecture licensing wherein all vendor counterparties are offered identical baseline consideration terms with time-window-stratified value-add layers, the vendor self-selecting the signing window.
- **Claim 2** — The method of Claim 1 wherein a stable cooperative-tier floor remains available to all vendor counterparties indefinitely, providing access to the open-source substrate and cooperative-defensive patent pledge without cash or equity consideration.
- **Claim 3** — The method of Claim 1 wherein vendor counterparties at non-floor tiers contribute both cash and equity consideration to the cooperative collective, the equity governed under cooperative pro-rata allocation mechanisms.
- **Claim 4** — The method of Claim 1 wherein vendor counterparties receive branded-fork rights subject to a member-portability covenant ensuring members retain rights to use the substrate via any vendor or via local inference.
- **Claim 5** — The method of Claim 1 integrated with a cooperative-defensive patent pledge such that all vendor counterparties sign the pledge as a precondition of any tier (including the stable cooperative-tier floor).
- **Claim 6** — The method of Claim 1 wherein cooperative-defensive patent enforcement against non-pledged infringers may be joined by all pledge-signing vendor counterparties under cooperative-defensive litigation terms.
- **Claim 7** — The method of Claim 1 implemented for substrate-grounded retrieval architectures producing empirically-measured retrieval-quality lift signatures (the Cathedral Effect family) across multiple commercial AI vendors.
- **Claim 8** — The method of Claim 1 wherein member substrate content remains member-owned and member-portable independent of any vendor counterparty's branded-fork rights or preview-window access.
